- diagnosis: The task is to assess the likely AIE mechanism for a large cationic, highly conjugated, donor-acceptor aromatic molecule. The current working top1 is ICT and the current runner-up is TICT. A further still-credible portfolio member is neutral aromatic because the scaffold is heavily aromatic and the available structure proxies indicate high planarity, so the case should not be collapsed immediately into a pure ICT-vs-TICT framing. Top1 is still uncertain because the present evidence is mostly motif-level and geometric proxy evidence rather than explicit excited-state localization or twisting evidence. Shared prepared structure context is available and ready, which enables bounded reuse by specialized agents. Macro can deterministically summarize one structural evidence family from the registry, but it cannot make a global mechanistic judgment or perform multi-step synthesis of all cues in one call. Microscopic can perform one low-cost baseline-only S0/S1 action on the shared structure, which may give indirect evidence about charge-transfer plausibility or brightness trends, but it cannot in round 1 resolve conformer sensitivity, torsion sensitivity, or full mechanism closure. Because both structural topology and baseline excited-state behavior matter here, the first round should gather both macro and microscopic evidence. The case remains in portfolio screening rather than pairwise contraction because TICT and neutral aromatic both still carry unresolved coverage debt.

### Round 2 | macro | run_macro

- agent_name: macro

- status: success

- task_received: Current reasoning phase: portfolio_screening. Agent framing mode: portfolio_neutral. Do not treat ICT as settled. Execute exactly one registry-backed macro capability: `screen_rotor_torsion_topology`. The purpose is to directly screen the still-credible TICT alternative relative to the current ICT lead by summarizing rotor density, torsion candidates, branching topology, and whether the observable structural picture provides bounded support, weakening, or unresolved status for TICT. Keep the report focused on screening coverage debt for TICT, not global mechanism adjudication.

- task_completion_status: completed

- task_completion: Task completed successfully within current macro capability.

- task_understanding: The task is to perform a bounded macro-level structural screening focused on the TICT hypothesis, which remains a credible alternative to the current ICT lead. The screening should summarize rotor density, torsion candidates, branching topology, and assess whether the structural evidence provides bounded support, weakening, or remains unresolved for TICT. This is to address the portfolio coverage debt for TICT without making any global mechanism adjudication or treating ICT as settled.

This involves analyzing the molecular structure to assess aromatic-core dominance, ring-system rigidity, and structural cues indicative of a neutral aromatic mechanism. The goal is to provide evidence that either supports keeping the neutral aromatic hypothesis credible alongside ICT/TICT or indicates that donor-acceptor polarization structurally suppresses the neutral aromatic interpretation. The screening must use exactly one registry-backed macro capability and leverage the shared prepared structure context if available.

The neutral aromatic hypothesis remains credible but untested by a dedicated macro structural screen. The molecule has a large aromatic core and high planarity proxy, suggesting potential aromatic-core dominance and ring-system rigidity. This screening will directly address the remaining coverage debt by evaluating these structural features to determine if neutral aromatic cues are strong enough to keep it competitive or if donor-acceptor effects dominate.

The screening is limited to structural evidence and cannot adjudicate global mechanism or excited-state behavior.
